       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Rouen_France_Panoramic-View-02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Rouen France Panoramic-View-02.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Rouen_France_Panoramic-View-02.jpg/220px-Rouen_France_Panoramic-View-02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Rouen_France_Panoramic-View-02.jpg/330px-Rouen_France_Panoramic-View-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Rouen_France_Panoramic-View-02.jpg/440px-Rouen_France_Panoramic-View-02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5732" data-file-height="3821"></a>

          <a href="/wiki/File:Rouen_France_Panoramic-View-02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>

      <p><b>France</b> (<span class="IPA audiolink nounderlines" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/51/En-us-France.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-France.ogg">/ˈfræns/</a></span> <span class="metadata audiolinkinfo"><small>(<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="extiw" title="w:Wikipedia:Media help">help</a>·<a href="/wiki/File:En-us-France.ogg" title="File:En-us-France.ogg">info</a>)</small></span> or <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/ˈfrɑːns/</span>; <small>French pronunciation:&nbsp;​</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[fʁɑ̃s]</a></span>), officially the <b>French Republic</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">République française</i>, <small>French pronunciation:&nbsp;​</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ʁepyblik fʁɑ̃sɛz]</a></span>), is a <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> whose <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_France" title="Metropolitan France">metropolitan territory</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a> and that also comprises various <a href="/w/index.php?title=Overseas_departments_and_territories_of_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Overseas departments and territories of France (not yet started)">overseas islands and territories located in other continents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CatTOM_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CatTOM-22">[10]</a></sup> Metropolitan France extends from the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> to the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>, and from the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>. It is often referred to as <i>L’Hexagone</i> ("The <a href="/wiki/Hexagon" title="Hexagon">Hexagon</a>") because of the shape of its territory. France is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> with its main ideals expressed in the <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_the_Rights_of_Man_and_of_the_Citizen" title="Declaration of the Rights of Man and of the Citizen">Declaration of the Rights of Man and of the Citizen</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_France" title="Metropolitan France">Metropolitan France</a> is bordered (clockwise from the north) by <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. The overseas departments and collectivities of France also share land borders with <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> (bordering <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a> (bordering <a href="/wiki/Saint-Martin" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Saint-Martin">Saint-Martin</a>). France is linked to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a>, which passes underneath the English Channel. </p>
      <p>France is the largest country in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the second largest in Europe. It has been one of the world's foremost <a href="/w/index.php?title=Power_in_international_relations&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Power in international relations (not yet started)">powers</a> for many centuries. During the 17th and 18th centuries, France colonized much of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>; during the 19th and early 20th centuries, France built <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">one of the largest colonial empires</a> of the time, including large portions of <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, and many <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific islands</a>. France is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a> and possesses the fifth largest <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Economy of France">economy</a><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[11]</a></sup> in the world, according to <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">nominal GDP figures</a>. It is the most visited country in the world, receiving 82 million foreign tourists annually.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism.stat_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism.stat-24">[12]</a></sup> France is one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, and has the largest land area of all members. It is also a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, and a member of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Francophonie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Francophonie (not yet started)">Francophonie</a>, the <a href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Latin Union (not yet started)">Latin Union</a>. It is one of the five permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> and owns the largest <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_with_nuclear_weapons&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="List of countries with nuclear weapons (not yet started)">number of nuclear weapons</a> with active warheads and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuclear_power_in_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nuclear power in France (not yet started)">nuclear power plants</a> in the European Union. </p>
      <p>France's official language is French, also being official in 29 other countries. Some other French speaking countries include Haiti, Cameroon, and Niger. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography and climate">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: Geography and climate">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>France is located in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[13]</a></sup> France shares its <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">borders</a> with <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kwintessential1_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kwintessential1-26">[14]</a></sup> France has two <a href="/wiki/Mountain" title="Mountain">mountain</a> ranges near its borders: the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> in the east and the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-kwintessential1_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kwintessential1-26">[14]</a></sup> There are many rivers in France, including the <a href="/wiki/Seine" title="Seine">Seine</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Loire_River" title="Loire River">Loire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[15]</a></sup> In the north and the west of France, there are low hills and river valleys. </p>
      <p>In France there are many different <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> has a major effect on the weather in the north and west. This means the temperature is about the same most of the year. It is in the marine west coast climate region. In the east, winters are cold and the <a href="/wiki/Weather" title="Weather">weather</a> is good. Summers are hot and stormy. In the south, winters are cool and <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">wet</a>. Summers are hot and dry.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[17]</a></sup> The north has a temperate climate similar to that of the United Kingdom and other Northern European countries. </p>
      <p>France has the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> (EEZ) in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[18]</a></sup> It covers 11,035,000 <a href="/wiki/Square_kilometre" title="Square kilometre">km<sup>2</sup></a> (4,260,637 <a href="/wiki/Square_miles" class="mw-redirect" title="Square miles">sq mi</a>). Only the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> has a larger one . </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name "France" comes from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> word Francia ', which means "land of the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The borders of modern France are about the same as those of ancient <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a>. <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celtic</a> Gauls inhabited Ancient Gaul. <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> conquered Gaul for <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Rome</a> in the 1st century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[20]</a></sup> Eventually, the Gauls adopted <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Roman</a> speech (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>, from which the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French language</a> evolved) and Roman culture. <a href="/wiki/History_of_Christianity" title="History of Christianity">Christianity</a> first appeared in the 2nd and 3rd centuries AD. It became firmly established by the fourth and fifth centuries. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_France_1477-fr.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Map_France_1477-fr.svg/220px-Map_France_1477-fr.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Map_France_1477-fr.svg/330px-Map_France_1477-fr.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Map_France_1477-fr.svg/440px-Map_France_1477-fr.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="970"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Map_France_1477-fr.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>France in 1477. Red line: Limit of the Kingdom of France; Light blue: the royal domain
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 4th century AD, the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribes</a>, principally the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a> invaded the Gauls. This is how the name <i>Francie</i> appeared. The modern name "France" comes from the name of the <a href="/wiki/Capetian_dynasty" title="Capetian dynasty">Capetian</a> Kings of France around Paris. The Franks were the first tribe of Europe after the fall of the Roman Empire to convert to Christianity rather than <a href="/wiki/Arianism" title="Arianism">Arianism</a>. The French called themselves "the most Christian Kingdom of France".<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun" title="Treaty of Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a> (843), divided <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">Empire</a> into three parts.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[22]</a></sup> The biggest area was Western Francia. It is similar to modern France. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Carolingian" class="mw-redirect" title="Carolingian">Carolingian</a> <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">dynasty</a> <a href="/wiki/Rule" title="Rule">ruled</a> France until 987, when <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Capet_of_France" title="Hugh Capet of France">Hugh Capet</a> became <a href="/wiki/King_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="King of France">King of France</a>. His descendants, the <a href="/wiki/Capetian_dynasty" title="Capetian dynasty">Direct Capetians</a>, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Valois" title="House of Valois">House of Valois</a> and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">House of Bourbon</a>, <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/unify" class="extiw" title="wikt:unify">unified</a> the country with many wars and dynastic inheritance. The monarchy was the most <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">powerful</a> during the 17th century and the reign of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV of France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[23]</a></sup> At that time, France had the <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographics of France">largest population in Europe</a>. The country had a big influence over European <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">politics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a>. <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> became the common language of <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomacy</a> in international affairs. Much of the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> happened in France. French scientists made big <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">scientific</a> discoveries in the 18th century. France also <a href="/wiki/Invasion" title="Invasion">conquered</a> many <a href="/wiki/French_overseas_collectivities" title="French overseas collectivities">overseas possessions</a> in the Americas and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>France had a <a href="/wiki/Monarchy" title="Monarchy">monarchy</a> until the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> in 1789. The Great King <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVI_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XVI of France">Louis XVI</a> and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Marie_Antoinette" title="Marie Antoinette">Marie Antoinette</a>, were <a href="/wiki/Executed" class="mw-redirect" title="Executed">executed</a> in 1793.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[25]</a></sup> Thousands of other French citizens were killed. <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> took control of the Republic in 1799. He later made himself Emperor of the First Empire (1804–1814). His armies conquered most of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">continental Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[26]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Metric_system" title="Metric system">metric system</a> was invented by French scientists during the French revolution.That time 3 estates were developed. </p>
      <p>After Napoleon's final defeat in 1815 at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a>, another monarchy arose. Later <a href="/wiki/Louis-Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis-Napoléon Bonaparte">Louis-Napoléon Bonaparte</a> created the Second Empire in 1852. Louis-Napoléon was removed after the defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-Prussian war">Franco-Prussian war</a> of 1870. The Third Republic replaced his <a href="/wiki/Regime" title="Regime">regime</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The large <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonial empire</a> in the 19th century included parts of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. The culture and politics of these regions were <a href="/wiki/Influence" title="Influence">influenced</a> by France. Many <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">ex-colonies</a> officially speak the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> language.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country actively took part in both the <a href="/wiki/WWI" class="mw-redirect" title="WWI">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/WWII" class="mw-redirect" title="WWII">Second World Wars</a>, with battles taking place on its soil. During the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, millions were killed in the trenches including over a million in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Battle of the Somme</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[29]</a></sup> The conditions were extremely difficult for the soldiers on the front. The last surviving veteran was Pierre Picault who died on 20 November 2008 at the age of 109.<sup id="cite_ref-France_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France-42">[30]</a></sup> During the Second World War, <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Nazis</a> <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/occupy" class="extiw" title="wikt:occupy">occupied</a> France. The Allies landed in Normandy on 6 June 1944 and began the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Normandy" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Normandy">Battle of Normandy</a>. German forces lost France in just a few months. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisions">Divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Divisions">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Divisions">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The 13 regions and 96 <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">departments</a> of <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_France" title="Metropolitan France">metropolitan France</a> include <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>. France is divided into (administrative) <a href="/wiki/Region" title="Region">regions</a>: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Auvergne-Rh%C3%B4ne-Alpes" title="Auvergne-Rhône-Alpes">Auvergne-Rhône-Alpes</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Bourgogne-Franche-Comt%C3%A9" title="Bourgogne-Franche-Comté">Bourgogne-Franche-Comté</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a> (<i>Bretagne</i>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Centre-Val_de_Loire" title="Centre-Val de Loire">Centre-Val de Loire</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a> (<i>Corse</i>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Grand_Est" title="Grand Est">Grand Est</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Hauts-de-France" title="Hauts-de-France">Hauts-de-France</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele-de-France" title="Île-de-France">Île-de-France</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a> (<i>Normandie</i>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Nouvelle-Aquitaine" title="Nouvelle-Aquitaine">Nouvelle-Aquitaine</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Occitanie" title="Occitanie">Occitanie</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Pays_de_la_Loire" title="Pays de la Loire">Pays de la Loire</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur">Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Corsica has a different status than the other 12 metropolitan regions. It is called <i><a href="/wiki/Collectivit%C3%A9_territoriale" class="mw-redirect" title="Collectivité territoriale">collectivité territoriale</a></i>. </p>
      <p>France also has five <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Regions_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Regions of France">overseas regions</a>: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> (in South America)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> (in the Caribbean)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> (in the Caribbean)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> (in the Indian Ocean)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> (in the Indian Ocean)</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>These four overseas regions have the same status as the metropolitan ones. They are like the overseas American states of <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. </p>
      <p>Then France is divided into 101 <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">departments</a>. The departments are divided into 342 <a href="/wiki/Arrondissements_of_France" title="Arrondissements of France">arrondissements</a>. The <i>arrondissements</i> are re-divided into 4,032 <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_France" title="Cantons of France">cantons</a>. The smallest <a href="/wiki/Administrative_division" title="Administrative division">subdivision</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">commune</a> (there are 36,699 communes). On January 1, 2008, <a href="/wiki/INSEE" title="INSEE">INSEE</a> counted 36,781 communes in France. 36,569 of them are in <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_France" title="Metropolitan France">metropolitan France</a> and 212 of them are in <a href="/wiki/Overseas_France" title="Overseas France">overseas France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Government">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: Government">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The government of France is a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential system</a> determined by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=French_Constitution&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="French Constitution (not yet started)">French Constitution</a> of the French Fifth <a href="/wiki/French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="French Republic">Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[33]</a></sup> The constitution declares the nation to be "an indivisible, <a href="/wiki/Secular" class="mw-redirect" title="Secular">secular</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democratic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Social" class="mw-redirect" title="Social">social</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">Republic</a>". It provides for a <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Military">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Military">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gaule96.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Gaule96.jpg/220px-Gaule96.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Gaule96.jpg/330px-Gaule96.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Gaule96.jpg/440px-Gaule96.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="443"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gaule96.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nuclear <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carrier</a> <i>Charles de Gaulle</i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:French_Republican_Guard_Bastille_Day_2007_n4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/French_Republican_Guard_Bastille_Day_2007_n4.jpg/170px-French_Republican_Guard_Bastille_Day_2007_n4.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/French_Republican_Guard_Bastille_Day_2007_n4.jpg/255px-French_Republican_Guard_Bastille_Day_2007_n4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/French_Republican_Guard_Bastille_Day_2007_n4.jpg/340px-French_Republican_Guard_Bastille_Day_2007_n4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="2390"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:French_Republican_Guard_Bastille_Day_2007_n4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>French Republican Guard
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The French <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> are divided into four branches: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The <i>Armée de Terre</i> (Army)</li> 
       <li>The <i>Marine Nationale</i> (Navy)</li> 
       <li>The <i>Armée de l'Air</i> (Air Force)</li> 
       <li>The <i>Gendarmerie Nationale</i> (A military force which acts as a <a href="/wiki/National" class="mw-redirect" title="National">National</a> <a href="/wiki/Rural" class="mw-redirect" title="Rural">Rural</a> <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">Police</a>)</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>France has about 359,000 military personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[36]</a></sup> France spends 2.6% of its <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) on <a href="/wiki/Defense_(military)" title="Defense (military)">defense</a>. This is the highest in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. France and the <a href="/wiki/UK" class="mw-redirect" title="UK">UK</a> spend 40% of the EU defence <a href="/wiki/Budget" title="Budget">budget</a>. About 10% of France's defence budget is for its <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear weapons</a> force. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Foreign relations">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: Foreign relations">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>
      </div> 
      <p>France is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[37]</a></sup> It is a permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> and has <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto</a> rights.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[38]</a></sup> It is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="World Trade Organisation">World Trade Organisation</a> (WTO). It hosts the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a>. In <a href="/wiki/1953" title="1953">1953</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> asked France to choose a <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> to represent them internationally. The French emblem is now on their <a href="/wiki/Passport" title="Passport">passports</a>. </p>
      <p>France was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[39]</a></sup> In the 1960s, France wanted to exclude the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation">organisation</a>. It wanted to build its own <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">economic</a> <a href="/wiki/Influence" title="Influence">power</a> in continental <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. France and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> became closer after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. This was to try to become the most influential country in the EU. It limited the influence of the new <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern European</a> members. France is a member of the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Treaty Organisation">North Atlantic Treaty Organisation</a> (NATO).<sup id="cite_ref-nato_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nato-52">[40]</a></sup> However, under <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">President de Gaulle</a>, it left the joint military command. In the early 1990s, France received <a href="/wiki/Criticism" title="Criticism">criticism</a> for its underground <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear</a> tests in <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>. France vigorously opposed the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[41]</a></sup> France retains strong political and economic influence in its former <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> colonies. For instance it has supplied economic aid and troops for peace-keeping missions in the <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Economy">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Economy">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:A380_Reveal_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/A380_Reveal_2.jpg/220px-A380_Reveal_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="75" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/A380_Reveal_2.jpg/330px-A380_Reveal_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/A380_Reveal_2.jpg/440px-A380_Reveal_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2098" data-file-height="716"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:A380_Reveal_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The first completed <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a> on 18 January 2005. Airbus is a symbol of the <a href="/wiki/Globalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Globalisation">globalisation</a> of the French and European economy.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>France is a member of the <a href="/wiki/G8" title="G8">G8</a> group of <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/lead#Verb" class="extiw" title="wikt:lead">leading</a> <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/industry" class="extiw" title="wikt:industry">industrialised</a> countries. France has the eighth-largest economy in the world by <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">Gross domestic product (GDP)</a> (which takes into account how much it costs to live in different countries and <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a> rates).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[42]</a></sup> France and 11 other <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> members jointly launched the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> on 1 January 1999 and started using it in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>France's economy has nearly 2.9 million registered companies.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[44]</a></sup> The government has a considerable influence over <a href="/wiki/Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway">railway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">electricity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a> firms (as it owns big companies like <a href="/w/index.php?title=SNCF&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SNCF (not yet started)">SNCF</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89lectricit%C3%A9_de_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Électricité de France (not yet started)">EDF</a> (French electricity)).<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[45]</a></sup> France has an important aerospace (design of <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a>) industry led by <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[46]</a></sup> It can also launch <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">rockets</a> from <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>France has invested a lot in <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a>. This made France the smallest producer of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">carbon dioxide</a> among the seven most industrialised countries in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[48]</a></sup> As a result, 59 nuclear power plants generate most of the electricity produced in the country (78% in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[49]</a></sup> up from only 8% in 1973, 24% in 1980, and 75% in 1990). </p>
      <p>France is the leading agricultural producer and exporter in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[50]</a></sup> France exports <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">poultry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dairy" class="mw-redirect" title="Dairy">dairy</a> products, <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a>. It is also famous for its <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> industry. France received 10 billion euros in 2006 from the European Community as <a href="/wiki/Subsidy" title="Subsidy">subsidies</a> to its farmers.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCCap_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCCap-63">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At one time, the Factory Act of 1833 limited the workday for women and children to 11&nbsp;hours a day.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Demographics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: Demographics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>On 1 January 2008, it was estimated that 63.8 million people live in France, including in the <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Regions_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Regions of France">Overseas Regions of France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-entire_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entire-65">[53]</a></sup> 61,875,000 of these live in metropolitan France, the part of the country that is within <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-entire_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entire-65">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Ethnic groups">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: Ethnic groups">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The major ethnic groups living in France today are descended from <a href="/wiki/Celt" class="mw-redirect" title="Celt">Celtic people</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USStateDeptBN_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USStateDeptBN-66">[54]</a></sup> The significant minority groups living in France are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Teutonic, that is <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a><sup id="cite_ref-USStateDeptBN_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USStateDeptBN-66">[54]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic</a><sup id="cite_ref-USStateDeptBN_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USStateDeptBN-66">[54]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>people from <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a><sup id="cite_ref-USStateDeptBN_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USStateDeptBN-66">[54]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>Sub-Saharan African - people from <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> who live south of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a> desert<sup id="cite_ref-USStateDeptBN_66-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USStateDeptBN-66">[54]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>people from <a href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a><sup id="cite_ref-USStateDeptBN_66-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USStateDeptBN-66">[54]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>people from the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country</a> of southwest Europe<sup id="cite_ref-USStateDeptBN_66-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USStateDeptBN-66">[54]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="***REMOVED***">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Language">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Language">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French language</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> is the official <a href="/wiki/Language" title="***REMOVED***">language</a> of France. It belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Romance_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romance language">Romance language</a> group, which includes <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>. Many regional <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a> are also used in France. <a href="/wiki/Alsatian_language" title="Alsatian language">Alsatian</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> dialect, is spoken in <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">Alsace</a> and in parts of <a href="/wiki/Lorraine" title="Lorraine">Lorraine</a> in eastern France. French was the language of <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomacy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> between the 17th and 19th century and is still widely used.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some people in France also speak <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsican_language" title="Corsican language">Corsican</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flemish_language" title="Flemish language">Flemish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Religion">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Change section: Religion">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>France is a <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">secular</a> country and the <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a> guarantees freedom of <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[56]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">population</a> is about 51% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, and 31% of people are <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnostics</a> or <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a>. 5% are <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a>, 3% say they are <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> and 1% say they are <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish</a>. 10% are from other religions or do not have an opinion about religion.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-religion_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religion-70">[58]</a></sup> There are also <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrian" class="mw-redirect" title="Zoroastrian">Zoroastrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Universalism" title="Unitarian Universalism">Unitarian Universalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wicca" title="Wicca">Wiccan</a> communities. Religions founded in France include <a href="/wiki/Raelism" class="mw-redirect" title="Raelism">Raelism</a>. </p>
      <p>According to a Poll in 2007:<sup id="cite_ref-EUROBAROMETER_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUROBAROMETER-71">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><b>34%</b> of French citizens responded that <i>"they believe there is a <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>"</i>.</li> 
       <li><b>27%</b> answered that <i>"they believe there is some sort of <a href="/wiki/Spirit" title="Spirit">spirit</a> or life force"</i>.</li> 
       <li><b>33%</b> answered that <i>"they do not believe there is any sort of spirit, God, or life force"</i>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Literature">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Change section: Literature">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_literature" title="French literature">French literature</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dartagnan-musketeers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Dartagnan-musketeers.jpg/220px-Dartagnan-musketeers.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="251" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Dartagnan-musketeers.jpg/330px-Dartagnan-musketeers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Dartagnan-musketeers.jpg/440px-Dartagnan-musketeers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dartagnan-musketeers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>The Three Musketeers</i> by <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Dumas,_p%C3%A8re" title="Alexandre Dumas, père">Alexandre Dumas</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>French literature began in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[60]</a></sup> French was divided into several dialects at the time. Some authors <a href="/wiki/Spelling" class="mw-redirect" title="Spelling">spelled</a> words differently from one other. </p>
      <p>During the 17th century, <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Corneille" title="Pierre Corneille">Pierre Corneille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean_Racine" title="Jean Racine">Jean Racine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moli%C3%A8re" title="Molière">Molière</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Pascal" title="Blaise Pascal">Blaise Pascal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Descartes" title="René Descartes">René Descartes</a> were the main authors.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 18th and 19th centuries, French literature and poetry reached its best. The 18th century saw writings of authors, <a href="/wiki/Essay" title="Essay">essayists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moral" class="mw-redirect" title="Moral">moralists</a> as <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Jean-Jacques Rousseau</a>. As for French children's literature in those times, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Perrault" title="Charles Perrault">Charles Perrault</a> wrote stories such as "<a href="/wiki/Little_Red_Riding_Hood" title="Little Red Riding Hood">Little Red Riding Hood</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Beauty_and_the_Beast" title="Beauty and the Beast">Beauty and the Beast</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Sleeping_Beauty" title="Sleeping Beauty">Sleeping Beauty</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Puss_in_Boots" title="Puss in Boots">Puss in Boots</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many famous French novels were written in the 19th century by authors such as <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugo" title="Victor Hugo">Victor Hugo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Dumas,_p%C3%A8re" title="Alexandre Dumas, père">Alexandre Dumas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne" title="Jules Verne">Jules Verne</a>. They wrote popular novels like <a href="/wiki/The_Three_Musketeers" title="The Three Musketeers">The Three Musketeers</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Count_of_Monte-Cristo" class="mw-redirect" title="The Count of Monte-Cristo">The Count of Monte-Cristo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Twenty_Thousand_Leagues_Under_the_Sea" title="Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea">Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hunchback_of_Notre-Dame" class="mw-redirect" title="The Hunchback of Notre-Dame">The Hunchback of Notre-Dame</a> and <a href="/wiki/Les_Mis%C3%A9rables" title="Les Misérables">Les Misérables</a>. Other 19th century fiction writers include <a href="/wiki/Emile_Zola" class="mw-redirect" title="Emile Zola">Emile Zola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guy_de_Maupassant" title="Guy de Maupassant">Guy de Maupassant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9ophile_Gautier" title="Théophile Gautier">Théophile Gautier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stendhal" title="Stendhal">Stendhal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Famous novels were written during the 20th century by <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Proust" title="Marcel Proust">Marcel Proust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antoine_de_Saint-Exup%C3%A9ry" title="Antoine de Saint-Exupéry">Antoine de Saint-Exupéry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Camus" title="Albert Camus">Albert Camus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Sartre" title="Jean-Paul Sartre">Jean-Paul Sartre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michel_Houellebecq" title="Michel Houellebecq">Michel Houellebecq</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=14" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Sports">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Change section: Sports">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:TourDeFrance_2005_07_09.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/TourDeFrance_2005_07_09.jpg/220px-TourDeFrance_2005_07_09.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/TourDeFrance_2005_07_09.jpg/330px-TourDeFrance_2005_07_09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/TourDeFrance_2005_07_09.jpg/440px-TourDeFrance_2005_07_09.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2143" data-file-height="1709"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:TourDeFrance_2005_07_09.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <i>Peloton</i> (means "pack" in French) of the <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a> <a href="/wiki/Cycling" class="mw-redirect" title="Cycling">cycling</a> <a href="/wiki/Racing" title="Racing">race</a> in July is one of the best-known <a href="/wiki/Sport" title="Sport">sporting</a> events.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[64]</a></sup> It is a three-week race of around 3,500&nbsp;km that covers most of France and ends in the centre of Paris, on the <i>Avenue des Champs-Elysées</i>. <a href="/wiki/Football_(soccer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Football (soccer)">Football</a> is another popular sport in France. The French team won the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in 1998 and 2018. They also won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Football_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA European Football Championship">UEFA European Football Championship</a> in 1984 and 2000. France also hosts the <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="24 Hours of Le Mans">24 Hours of Le Mans</a> <a href="/wiki/Car_race" class="mw-redirect" title="Car race">car race</a>. France also hosted the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_World_Cup" title="Rugby World Cup">Rugby World Cup</a> in 2007 and finished fourth.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[65]</a></sup> France is closely associated with the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Modern Olympic Games</a>. At the end of the 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Baron" title="Baron">Baron</a> <a href="/wiki/Pierre_de_Coubertin" title="Pierre de Coubertin">Pierre de Coubertin</a> suggested having the Olympic Games again. France hosted the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> twice, in 1900 and 1924, in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. France will host the Summer Olympics in 2024, in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. France also hosted the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Games</a> three times: in 1924 in <a href="/wiki/Chamonix" title="Chamonix">Chamonix</a>, in 1968 in <a href="/wiki/Grenoble" title="Grenoble">Grenoble</a>, and in 1992 in <a href="/wiki/Albertville" title="Albertville">Albertville</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=15" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Cuisine">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Change section: Cuisine">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG/230px-Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG" decoding="async" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG/345px-Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG/460px-Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Terrine_de_saumon_au_basilic.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Basil salmon <a href="/w/index.php?title=Terrine_(food)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Terrine (food) (not yet started)">terrine</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>French cuisine has influenced the style of cooking throughout Europe, and its chefs work in restaurants throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The roots of modern <i>haute cuisine</i> lie in chefs like <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Pierre_La_Varenne" title="François Pierre La Varenne">La Varenne</a> (1615–1678) and the notable chef of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marie-Antoine_Car%C3%AAme" title="Marie-Antoine Carême">Marie-Antoine Carême</a> (1784–1833). These chefs developed a lighter style of food compared to the food of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. They used fewer spices, and more <a href="/wiki/Herb" title="Herb">herbs</a> and creamy ingredients. </p>
      <p>Typical ingredients like <a href="/wiki/Roux" title="Roux">roux</a> and fish stock, and techniques such as <a href="/wiki/Marinade" title="Marinade">marinading</a>, and dishes such as <a href="/wiki/Ragout" title="Ragout">ragout</a>, were invented. Carême was an expert pâtissier (pastry-maker), and this is still a mark of French cooking. He developed basic sauces, his 'mother sauces'; he had over a hundred sauces in his repertoire, based on the half-dozen mother sauces. </p>
      <p>French cuisine was introduced in the 20th century by <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Escoffier" title="Auguste Escoffier">Georges Auguste Escoffier</a> (1846–1935). He was a genius at organisation. He worked out how to run large restaurants, as in a big hotel or a palace; how the staff should be organised; how the menu was prepared. He had methods for everything. Escoffier's largest contribution was the publication of <i>Le Guide Culinaire</i> in 1903, which established the fundamentals of French cookery. Escoffier managed the restaurants and cuisine at the <a href="/wiki/Savoy_Hotel" title="Savoy Hotel">Savoy Hotel</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Carlton_Hotel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carlton Hotel (not yet started)">Carlton Hotel</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, the <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B4tel_Ritz_Paris" title="Hôtel Ritz Paris">Hôtel Ritz Paris</a>, and some of the greatest cruise ships. </p>
      <p>Escoffier, however, left out much of the culinary character to be found in the <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_France" title="Regions of France">regions of France</a>. </p>
      <p>Gastro-tourism and the <i><a href="/wiki/Guide_Michelin" class="mw-redirect" title="Guide Michelin">Guide Michelin</a></i> helped to make people familiar with the rich <a href="/wiki/Bourgeois" class="mw-redirect" title="Bourgeois">bourgeois</a> and peasant cuisine of the French countryside in the 20th century. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gascony&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gascony (not yet started)">Gascon</a> cuisine has also had great influence over the cuisine in the southwest of France. Many dishes that were once regional have become common all over the country. <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">Cheese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> are a major part of the cuisine, playing different roles regionally and nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[69]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/North" title="North">north</a> of France, people often prefer to use <a href="/wiki/Butter" title="Butter">butter</a> to <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/cook" class="extiw" title="wikt:cook">cook</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/South" title="South">south</a>, they prefer <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Garlic" title="Garlic">garlic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[70]</a></sup> In France, each <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_France" title="Regions of France">region</a> has its own special <a href="/wiki/Dish" title="Dish">dish</a>; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Choucroute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Choucroute (not yet started)">choucroute</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">Alsace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quiche" title="Quiche">quiche</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lorraine" title="Lorraine">Lorraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassoulet" title="Cassoulet">cassoulet</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Languedoc-Roussillon" title="Languedoc-Roussillon">Languedoc-Roussillon</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tapenade&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tapenade (not yet started)">tapenade</a> in <a href="/wiki/Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur">Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur</a>. </p>
      <p>In November 2010, <b>French gastronomy</b> was added by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> to its lists of the world's 'intangible cultural heritage'.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=16" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Tourism">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Change section: Tourism">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chateau-de-versailles-cour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Chateau-de-versailles-cour.jpg/220px-Chateau-de-versailles-cour.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Chateau-de-versailles-cour.jpg/330px-Chateau-de-versailles-cour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Chateau-de-versailles-cour.jpg/440px-Chateau-de-versailles-cour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1278" data-file-height="542"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chateau-de-versailles-cour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">Palace of Versailles</a> is one of the most popular tourist destinations in France.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>France is the number one <a href="/wiki/Tourist" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourist">tourist</a> destination in the world. In 2007, 81.9 million foreign tourists visited France.<sup id="cite_ref-gouv2007_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gouv2007-85">[73]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> comes second (58.5 million in 2006) and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> come third (51.1 million in 2006). Some of the most famous attractions in Paris, are the <a href="/wiki/Eiffel_Tower" title="Eiffel Tower">Eiffel Tower</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arc_de_Triomphe" title="Arc de Triomphe">Arc de Triomphe</a>. Another one is <a href="/wiki/Mont_Saint_Michel" class="mw-redirect" title="Mont Saint Michel">Mont Saint Michel</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A European <a href="/wiki/Disneyland" title="Disneyland">Disneyland</a> is located in a <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">suburb</a> east of Paris. The resort opened in 1992 and is also a popular tourist destination in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=19" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Notes">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=France&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Change section: Notes">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: upper-roman;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-one-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-one_1-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">For information about regional languages, see <a href="/w/index.php?title=Languages_of_France&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Languages of France (not yet started)">Languages of France</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-4">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Established the <a href="/wiki/West_Francia" title="West Francia">Kingdom of the West Franks</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a>) from the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Carolingian Empire</a> of Francia.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-5">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> since 1993.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-6">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Established the <a href="/wiki/French_Fifth_Republic" title="French Fifth Republic">Fifth Republic</a></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-three-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-three_8-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">French <a href="/w/index.php?title=Institut_G%C3%A9ographique_National&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Institut Géographique National (not yet started)">National Geographic Institute</a> data, which includes bodies of water.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-four-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-four_9-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">French <a href="/w/index.php?title=Land_registration&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Land registration (not yet started)">Land Register</a> data, which exclude lakes, ponds and <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a> larger than 1&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (0.386&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi or 247&nbsp;acres) as well as the estuaries of rivers.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-six-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-six_16-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Whole of the French Republic except the overseas territories in the Pacific Ocean.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-seven-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-seven_17-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">French overseas territories in the Pacific Ocean only.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-nine-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-nine_18-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Time zones across the French Republic span from UTC-10 (<a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a>) to UTC+12 (<a href="/wiki/Wallis_and_Futuna" title="Wallis and Futuna">Wallis and Futuna</a>).</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-eight-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-eight_19-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Daylight saving time is observed in metropolitan France and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Pierre_and_Miquelon" title="Saint Pierre and Miquelon">Saint Pierre and Miquelon</a> only.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-eleven-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-eleven_20-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">The overseas regions and collectivities form part of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=French_telephone_numbering_plan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="French telephone numbering plan (not yet started)">French telephone numbering plan</a>, but have their own country calling codes: <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> +590; <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> +596; <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> +594, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> +262; <a href="/wiki/Saint_Pierre_and_Miquelon" title="Saint Pierre and Miquelon">Saint Pierre and Miquelon</a> +508. The overseas territories are not part of the French telephone numbering plan; their country calling codes are: <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> +687, <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a> +689; <a href="/wiki/Wallis_and_Futuna" title="Wallis and Futuna">Wallis and Futuna</a> +681.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-ten-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-ten_21-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to <a href="/wiki/.fr" class="mw-redirect" title=".fr">.fr</a>, several other Internet TLDs are used in French overseas <i>départements</i> and territories: <a href="/wiki/.re" class="mw-redirect" title=".re">.re</a>, <a href="/wiki/.mq" class="mw-redirect" title=".mq">.mq</a>, <a href="/wiki/.gp" class="mw-redirect" title=".gp">.gp</a>, <a href="/wiki/.tf" class="mw-redirect" title=".tf">.tf</a>, <a href="/wiki/.nc" class="mw-redirect" title=".nc">.nc</a>, <a href="/wiki/.pf" class="mw-redirect" title=".pf">.pf</a>, <a href="/wiki/.wf" class="mw-redirect" title=".wf">.wf</a>, <a href="/wiki/.pm" class="mw-redirect" title=".pm">.pm</a>, <a href="/wiki/.gf" class="mw-redirect" title=".gf">.gf</a> and <a href="/wiki/.yt" class="mw-redirect" title=".yt">.yt</a>. France also uses <a href="/wiki/.eu" class="mw-redirect" title=".eu">.eu</a>, shared with other members of the European Union. The <a href="/wiki/.cat" class="mw-redirect" title=".cat">.cat</a> domain is used in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_Countries&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Catalan Countries (not yet started)">Catalan-speaking territories</a>.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
